## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermodynamics of polymers
**Analysis**: This task likely belongs to the thermodynamics of polymers because it involves the relationship between stress, strain, and temperature, which are all important factors in understanding the behavior of polymers. The task may also involve rheology and viscoelasticity.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Thermal stress: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - epsilon0) * (1 + c1 * T)
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (possibly related to stress relaxation or creep)
- WLF equation: c2 = c0 * exp(c1 / (T - c3)) * exp(c4 * epsilon) ( possibly related to viscoelastic behavior)
- Model for thermal expansion: c1 = c0 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon
- Lindemann theory: nu = c0 * exp(-c1 / T) (possibly related to stress relaxation or creep)
- Thermal-activated flow equation: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 / T) * (epsilon - epsilon_c) (possibly related to thermally activated flow in polymers)
- Stress-temperature relationship in polymers: sigma = c0 * T^c1 + c2 * epsilon
- Viscoelastic stress relaxation: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * t) + c2 * exp(-c3 * t) * epsilon
- Thermal stress in polymers: sigma = c0 * T * epsilon
- Eyring equation: v = c0 * exp(-c1 / T) * sin(c2 * epsilon) (possibly related to thermally activated flow in polymers)
- Thermal activation energy: E = c0 + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon
- Time-temperature superposition principle: c1 = c0 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon
- Thermal expansion: c1 = c0 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon
- Constitutive equation for polymers: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * d epsilon/dt + c2 * epsilon^2
- Strain-rate-dependent stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (d epsilon/dt)^c1 + c2 * epsilon^c3

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Hardening behavior → Power-law increase in stress with strain (sigma = c0 * epsilon^c1)
- Thermal activation → Exponential decrease in activation energy with increasing temperature (E = c0 * exp(-c1 / T))
- Strain-rate sensitivity → Dependence of stress on strain rate (sigma = c0 * epsilon * (d epsilon/dt)^c1)
- Stress-relaxation behavior → Exponential decay of stress with time (sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * t))
- Viscoelastic behavior → Combination of elastic and viscous contributions to stress (sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * d epsilon/dt)
- Thermal expansion → Linear or nonlinear increase in strain with temperature (epsilon = c0 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon^2)
- Thermally activated flow → Exponential dependence of flow rate on temperature (v = c0 * exp(-c1 / T))
- Gelation behavior → Sudden increase in stress as temperature is increased beyond a critical value (sigma = c0 * T^c1 for T > T_c)
- Softening behavior → Decrease in stress with increasing temperature (sigma = c0 - c1 * T)
